[1m(ูข) ุฃุนูุงู ุนู ุฑููุงู ุจุงุฑุช [0m

There are now many books on Barthes. Those mentioned below are just a selection. Louis-Jean Calvetโs [3mRoland Barthes [0m(Flammarion, 
1990), translated by Sarah Wykes, [3mRoland Barthes, A Biography [0m(Indiana University Press, 1995), is a lively biography with lots of 
information about Barthesโs friendships and opinions but which treats theories as feeble attempts to rationalize feelings. 

[1mูุชุจ ุจุงููุบุฉ ุงูุฅูุฌููุฒูุฉ [0m

Annette Laversโ early [3mRoland Barthes: Structuralism and After [0m(Harvard University Press, 1982) can be supplemented by Michael 
Moriartyโs [3mRoland Barthes [0m(Polity Press, 1991), a clear overview, especially helpful on Barthesโs dealings with Brecht and with 
narrative, and Stephen Ungarโs [3mRoland Barthes: The Professor of Desire [0m(University of Nebraska Press, 1983), which shrewdly charts 
Barthesโs shifting commitments and his appeal. More specialized are Andrew Brownโs [3mRoland Barthes: The Figures of Writing [0m(Oxford 
University Press, 1992), a study of major concerns and operations in Barthesโs writing; Armine Kotin Mortimer, [3mThe Gentlest Law: 
Roland Barthesโs โThe Pleasure of the Textโ, [0man exemplary, multi-dimensional reading of this book; and Diana Knightโs [3mBarthes and 
Utopia: Space, Travel, Writing [0m(Oxford University Press, 1997), a subtle exploration of the forms of the important utopian impulse 
in Barthesโs writing. D. A. Millerโs [3mBringing out Barthes [0m(University of California Press, 1992) obliquely but boldly evokes the 
gay Barthes that might have been. 

[1mูุชุจ ุจุงููุบุฉ ุงููุฑูุณูุฉ [0m

Stephen Heathโs early [3mVertige du dรฉplacement: Lecture de Barthes [0m(Fayard, 1974) is still smart and pertinent. Philippe Rogerโs [3m
Roland Barthes: roman [0m(Grasset, 1986) is a life and works particularly strong on Barthesโs formative experiences. It is devoted to 
the proposition that from the outset Barthes sought to make knowledge literary. Vincent Jouveโs [3mLa Littรฉrature selon Barthes [0m
(Minuit, 1986) is an attempt at theoretical synthesis of Barthesโs account of literature. Bernard Commentโs excellent [3mRoland 
Barthes: vers le neutre [0m(Christian Bourgois, 1991) finds a coherent project in the utopian attempt to escape from constraints of 
critical as well as orthodox thinking. 

[1mุฃุนูุงู ุฃุฎุฑู [0m

[3mPrรฉtexte: Roland Barthes [0m(Union gรฉnรฉrale dโรฉditions, 1978) is the proceedings of a conference on Barthes at Cรฉrisy, in which 
Barthes took an active part. [3mParagraph [0m11:2 (1988), [3mBarthes aprรจs Barthes, [0med. Cathrine Coquio and Regis Salado (Publications de 
lโUniversitรฉ de Pau, 1993), and [3mThe Yale Journal of Criticism [0m(fall 2001) collect papers from other conferences on Barthes. 

Numerous journals have devoted special issues to Barthes: [3mTel Quel [0m47 (autumn 1971), [3mCritique [0m302 (January 1972), [3mArc [0m56 (1974), [3m
Visible Language [0m(autumn 1977), [3mStudies in Twentieth-Century Literature [0m(spring 1981), [3mPoรฉtique [0m47 (September 1981), [3m
Communications [0m63 (1996), and [3mNottingham French Studies [0m(spring 1997). 

A parody of Barthes by Michel-Antoine Burnier and Patrick Rambaud, [3mLe Roland-Barthes sans peine [0m(Ballard, 1978), has rewarding 
moments. For further discussion of Barthes in the context of French structuralism, see Jonathan Culler, [3mStructuralist Poetics: 
Structuralism, Linguistics and the Study of Literature [0m(Cornell University Press, 1975).
